         <div class="plainlist">

      <p>
       <b>
        Jamaica
       </b>
       (
       <span class="nowrap">
        <span class="IPA nopopups noexcerpt">
         <a href="/wiki/Help:IPA/English" title="Help:IPA/English">
          /
          <span style="border-bottom:1px dotted">
           <span title="/dʒ/: 'j' in 'jam'">
            dʒ
           </span>
           <span title="/ə/: 'a' in 'about'">
            ə
           </span>
           <span title="/ˈ/: primary stress follows">
            ˈ
           </span>
           <span title="'m' in 'my'">
            m
           </span>
           <span title="/eɪ/: 'a' in 'face'">
            eɪ
           </span>
           <span title="'k' in 'kind'">
            k
           </span>
           <span title="/ə/: 'a' in 'about'">
            ə
           </span>
          </span>
          /
         </a>
        </span>
        <small class="nowrap">
         (
         <span class="unicode haudio">
          <span class="fn">
           <span style="white-space:nowrap">
            <a href="/wiki/File:En-us-Jamaica.ogg" title="About this sound">
             <img alt="About this sound" data-file-height="20" data-file-width="20" height="11" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/8/8a/Loudspeaker.svg/11px-Loudspeaker.svg.png" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/8/8a/Loudspeaker.svg/17px-Loudspeaker.svg.png 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/8/8a/Loudspeaker.svg/22px-Loudspeaker.svg.png 2x" width="11"/>
            </a>
           </span>
           <a class="internal" href="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/0/0a/En-us-Jamaica.ogg" title="En-us-Jamaica.ogg">
            listen
           </a>
          </span>
         </span>
         )
        </small>
       </span>
       ) is an
       <a href="/wiki/Island_country" title="Island country">
        island country
       </a>
       situated in the
       <a href="/wiki/Caribbean_Sea" title="Caribbean Sea">
        Caribbean Sea
       </a>
       . Spanning 10,990 square kilometres (4,240 sq mi) in area, it is the third-largest island of the
       <a href="/wiki/Greater_Antilles" title="Greater Antilles">
        Greater Antilles
       </a>
       and the fourth-largest island country in the
       <a href="/wiki/Caribbean" title="Caribbean">
        Caribbean
       </a>
       . Jamaica lies about 145 kilometres (90 mi) south of
       <a href="/wiki/Cuba" title="Cuba">
        Cuba
       </a>
       , and 191 kilometres (119 mi) west of
       <a href="/wiki/Hispaniola" title="Hispaniola">
        Hispaniola
       </a>
       (the island containing the countries of
       <a href="/wiki/Haiti" title="Haiti">
        Haiti
       </a>
       and the
       <a href="/wiki/Dominican_Republic" title="Dominican Republic">
        Dominican Republic
       </a>
       ).
      </p>
      <p>
       Previously inhabited by the indigenous
       <a href="/wiki/Arawak" title="Arawak">
        Arawak
       </a>
       and
       <a href="/wiki/Ta%C3%ADno" title="Taíno">
        Taíno
       </a>
       peoples, the island came under
       <a href="/wiki/Spanish_Empire" title="Spanish Empire">
        Spanish rule
       </a>
       following the arrival of
       <a href="/wiki/Christopher_Columbus" title="Christopher Columbus">
        Christopher Columbus
       </a>
       in 1494. Many of the indigenous people died of disease, and the Spanish transplanted African slaves to Jamaica as labourers. Named
       <i>
        <span lang="es">
         Santiago
        </span>
       </i>
       , the island remained a possession of Spain until 1655, when England (later
       <a href="/wiki/Kingdom_of_Great_Britain" title="Kingdom of Great Britain">
        Great Britain
       </a>
       ) conquered it and renamed it Jamaica. Under British colonial rule Jamaica became a leading sugar exporter, with its plantation economy highly dependent on slaves forcibly transported from Africa. The British fully emancipated all slaves in 1838, and many freedmen chose to have
       <a href="/wiki/Subsistence_agriculture" title="Subsistence agriculture">
        subsistence farms
       </a>
       rather than to work on plantations. Beginning in the 1840s, the British utilized Chinese and Indian
       <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Indentured" title="Indentured">
        indentured
       </a>
       labour to work on plantations. The island achieved independence from the United Kingdom on 6 August 1962.
      </p>
      <p>
       With 2.9 million people,
       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-UN_WPP_3-1">
        <a href="#cite_note-UN_WPP-3">
         [3]
        </a>
       </sup>
       Jamaica is the third-most populous
       <a href="/wiki/English-speaking_world" title="English-speaking world">
        Anglophone
       </a>
       country in the
       <a href="/wiki/Americas" title="Americas">
        Americas
       </a>
       (after the United States and Canada), and the fourth-most populous country in the Caribbean.
       <a href="/wiki/Kingston,_Jamaica" title="Kingston, Jamaica">
        Kingston
       </a>
       is the country's capital and largest city, with a population of 937,700.
       <a href="/wiki/Jamaicans" title="Jamaicans">
        Jamaicans
       </a>
       predominately have African ancestry, with significant
       <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/European_Jamaicans" title="European Jamaicans">
        European
       </a>
       ,
       <a href="/wiki/Chinese_Jamaicans" title="Chinese Jamaicans">
        Chinese
       </a>
       ,
       <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Indo-Jamaican" title="Indo-Jamaican">
        Indian
       </a>
       , and mixed-race minorities. Due to a high rate of emigration for work since the 1960s, Jamaica has a
       <a href="/wiki/Jamaican_diaspora" title="Jamaican diaspora">
        large diaspora
       </a>
       around the world, particularly in Canada, the United Kingdom, and the United States.
      </p>
      <p>
       Jamaica is a
       <a href="/wiki/Commonwealth_realm" title="Commonwealth realm">
        Commonwealth realm
       </a>
       , with
       <a href="/wiki/Elizabeth_II" title="Elizabeth II">
        Queen Elizabeth II
       </a>
       as
       <a href="/wiki/Monarchy_of_Jamaica" title="Monarchy of Jamaica">
        its monarch
       </a>
       and
       <a href="/wiki/Head_of_state" title="Head of state">
        head of state
       </a>
       . Her appointed representative in the country is the
       <a href="/wiki/Governor-General_of_Jamaica" title="Governor-General of Jamaica">
        Governor-General of Jamaica
       </a>
       , an office held by
       <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Patrick_Allen_(Governor-General)" title="Patrick Allen (Governor-General)">
        Sir Patrick Allen
       </a>
       since 2009.
       <a href="/wiki/Andrew_Holness" title="Andrew Holness">
        Andrew Holness
       </a>
       has served as the
       <a href="/wiki/Head_of_government" title="Head of government">
        head of government
       </a>
       and
       <a href="/wiki/Prime_Minister_of_Jamaica" title="Prime Minister of Jamaica">
        Prime Minister of Jamaica
       </a>
       from March 2016. Jamaica is a parliamentary
       <a href="/wiki/Constitutional_monarchy" title="Constitutional monarchy">
        constitutional monarchy
       </a>
       with legislative power vested in the bicameral
       <a href="/wiki/Parliament_of_Jamaica" title="Parliament of Jamaica">
        Parliament of Jamaica
       </a>
       , consisting of an appointed Senate and a directly elected House of Representatives.
      </p>
      <div class="thumb tright">
       <div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;">
        <a class="image" href="/wiki/File:Jm-map.png">
         <img alt="" class="thumbimage" data-file-height="340" data-file-width="670" height="112" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/d/dd/Jm-map.png/220px-Jm-map.png" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/d/dd/Jm-map.png/330px-Jm-map.png 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/d/dd/Jm-map.png/440px-Jm-map.png 2x" width="220"/>
        </a>
        <div class="thumbcaption">
         <div class="magnify">
          <a class="internal" href="/wiki/File:Jm-map.png" title="Enlarge">
          </a>
         </div>
         A map of Jamaica
        </div>
       </div>

         <ul>
          <li class="toclevel-2 tocsection-3">

          </li>
          <li class="toclevel-2 tocsection-4">
           <a href="#Spanish_rule_(1509–1655)">

           </a>
          </li>

      <p>
      </p>
      <h2>
       <span class="mw-headline" id="Etymology">
        Etymology
       </span>
      </h2>
      <p>
       The
       <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Indigenous_people" title="Indigenous people">
        indigenous people
       </a>
       , the
       <a href="/wiki/Ta%C3%ADno" title="Taíno">
        Taíno
       </a>
       , called the island
       <i>
        Xaymaca
       </i>
       in
       <a href="/wiki/Arawakan_languages" title="Arawakan languages">
        Arawakan
       </a>
       ,
       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-8">
        <a href="#cite_note-8">
         [8]
        </a>
       </sup>
       meaning the "Land of Wood and Water" or the "Land of Springs".
       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-taino_9-0">
        <a href="#cite_note-taino-9">
         [9]
        </a>
       </sup>
      </p>
      <p>
       Colloquially Jamaicans refer to their home island as the "Rock." Slang names such as "Jamrock", "Jamdown" ("Jamdung" in
       <a href="/wiki/Jamaican_Patois" title="Jamaican Patois">
        Jamaican Patois
       </a>
       ), or briefly "Ja", have derived from this.
       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-10">
        <a href="#cite_note-10">
         [10]
        </a>
       </sup>
      </p>
      <h2>
       <span class="mw-headline" id="History">
        History
       </span>
      </h2>
      <div class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable" role="note">
       Main article:
       <a href="/wiki/History_of_Jamaica" title="History of Jamaica">
        History of Jamaica
       </a>
      </div>
      <h3>
       <span class="mw-headline" id="Prehistory">
        Prehistory
       </span>
      </h3>
      <div class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable" role="note">
       Main article:
       <a href="/wiki/Pre-Columbian_Jamaica" title="Pre-Columbian Jamaica">
        Pre-Columbian Jamaica
       </a>
      </div>
      <p>
       The
       <a href="/wiki/Arawak" title="Arawak">
        Arawak
       </a>
       and
       <a href="/wiki/Ta%C3%ADno" title="Taíno">
        Taíno
       </a>
       indigenous people, originating in
       <a href="/wiki/South_America" title="South America">
        South America
       </a>
       , settled on the island between 4000 and 1000 BC.
       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-primearticles1_11-0">
        <a href="#cite_note-primearticles1-11">
         [11]
        </a>
       </sup>
       When
       <a href="/wiki/Christopher_Columbus" title="Christopher Columbus">
        Christopher Columbus
       </a>
       arrived in 1494, there were more than 200 villages ruled by
       <i>
        caciques
       </i>
       (chiefs of villages). The south coast of Jamaica was the most populated, especially around the area now known as Old Harbour.
       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-primearticles1_11-1">
        <a href="#cite_note-primearticles1-11">
         [11]
        </a>
       </sup>
       The Taino still inhabited Jamaica when the English took control of the island in 1655.
       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-primearticles1_11-2">
        <a href="#cite_note-primearticles1-11">
         [11]
        </a>
       </sup>
       The Jamaican National Heritage Trust is attempting to locate and document any evidence of the Taino/
       <a href="/wiki/Arawak" title="Arawak">
        Arawak
       </a>
       .
       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-12">
        <a href="#cite_note-12">
         [12]
        </a>
       </sup>
      </p>
      <h3>
       <span id="Spanish_rule_.281509.E2.80.931655.29">
       </span>
       <span class="mw-headline" id="Spanish_rule_(1509–1655)">
        Spanish rule (1509–1655)
       </span>
      </h3>
      <div class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable" role="note">
       Main article:
       <a href="/wiki/Colony_of_Santiago" title="Colony of Santiago">
        Colony of Santiago
       </a>
      </div>
      <p>
       Christopher Columbus claimed Jamaica for Spain after landing there in 1494. His probable landing point was Dry Harbour, called
       <a href="/wiki/Discovery_Bay,_Jamaica" title="Discovery Bay, Jamaica">
        Discovery Bay
       </a>
       ,
       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-columbus_13-0">
        <a href="#cite_note-columbus-13">
         [13]
        </a>
       </sup>
       <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Saint_Ann_Parish,_Jamaica" title="Saint Ann Parish, Jamaica">
        St. Ann's Bay
       </a>
       was named "Saint Gloria" by Columbus, as the first sighting of the land. One and a half kilometres west of St. Ann's Bay is the site of the first Spanish settlement on the island,
       <a href="/wiki/Sevilla_la_Nueva_(Jamaica)" title="Sevilla la Nueva (Jamaica)">
        Sevilla
       </a>
       , which was established in 1509 and abandoned around 1524 because it was deemed unhealthy.
       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-JNHT_14-0">
        <a href="#cite_note-JNHT-14">
         [14]
        </a>
       </sup>
       The capital was moved to
       <a href="/wiki/Spanish_Town" title="Spanish Town">
        Spanish Town
       </a>
       , then called
       <i>
        St. Jago de la Vega
       </i>
       , around 1534 (at present-day St. Catherine).
       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Spanish_town_15-0">
        <a href="#cite_note-Spanish_town-15">
         [15]
        </a>
       </sup>
      </p>
      <h3>
       <span id="British_rule_.281655.E2.80.931962.29">
       </span>
       <span class="mw-headline" id="British_rule_(1655–1962)">
        British rule (1655–1962)
       </span>
      </h3>
      <div class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable" role="note">
       Main article:
       <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/English_Jamaica" title="English Jamaica">
        English Jamaica
       </a>
      </div>
      <p>
       <a href="/wiki/Spanish_Town" title="Spanish Town">
        Spanish Town
       </a>
       has the oldest
       <a href="/wiki/Cathedral" title="Cathedral">
        cathedral
       </a>
       of the British colonies in the Caribbean.
       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Spanish_town_15-1">
        <a href="#cite_note-Spanish_town-15">
         [15]
        </a>
       </sup>
       The Spanish were forcibly evicted by the English at
       <a href="/wiki/Ocho_Rios" title="Ocho Rios">
        Ocho Rios
       </a>
       in St. Ann. In the 1655
       <a href="/wiki/Invasion_of_Jamaica" title="Invasion of Jamaica">
        Invasion of Jamaica
       </a>
       , the English, led by
       <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/William_Penn_(admiral)" title="William Penn (admiral)">
        Sir William Penn
       </a>
       and General
       <a href="/wiki/Robert_Venables" title="Robert Venables">
        Robert Venables
       </a>
       , took over the last Spanish fort on the island.
       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-jamsenghist_16-0">
        <a href="#cite_note-jamsenghist-16">
         [16]
        </a>
       </sup>
       The name of Montego Bay, the capital of the parish of St. James, was derived from the Spanish name
       <i>
        <span lang="es">
         manteca bahía
        </span>
       </i>
       (or Bay of Lard), alluding to the lard-making industry based on processing the numerous
       <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Boars" title="Boars">
        boars
       </a>
       in the area.
       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-17">
        <a href="#cite_note-17">
         [17]
        </a>
       </sup>
      </p>
      <div class="thumb tright">
       <div class="thumbinner" style="width:172px;">
        <a class="image" href="/wiki/File:Morgan,Henry.jpg">
         <img alt="" class="thumbimage" data-file-height="760" data-file-width="597" height="216" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/3/3a/Morgan%2CHenry.jpg/170px-Morgan%2CHenry.jpg" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/3/3a/Morgan%2CHenry.jpg/255px-Morgan%2CHenry.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/3/3a/Morgan%2CHenry.jpg/340px-Morgan%2CHenry.jpg 2x" width="170"/>
        </a>
        <div class="thumbcaption">
         <div class="magnify">
          <a class="internal" href="/wiki/File:Morgan,Henry.jpg" title="Enlarge">
          </a>
         </div>
         <a href="/wiki/Henry_Morgan" title="Henry Morgan">
          Henry Morgan
         </a>
         was a famous
         <a href="/wiki/Piracy_in_the_Caribbean" title="Piracy in the Caribbean">
          Caribbean pirate
         </a>
         and privateer; he had first come to the West Indies as an indentured servant, like most of the early English colonists.
         <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-18">
          <a href="#cite_note-18">
           [18]
          </a>
         </sup>
        </div>
       </div>
      </div>
      <p>
       The English continued to "import" African slaves as labourers.
      </p>
      <p>
       In 1660, the population of Jamaica was about 4,500 white and 1,500 black.
       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-population_19-0">
        <a href="#cite_note-population-19">
         [19]
        </a>
       </sup>
       By the early 1670s, as the English developed sugar cane plantations and "imported" more slaves, black people formed a majority of the population.
       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-20">
        <a href="#cite_note-20">
         [20]
        </a>
       </sup>
       The colony was shaken and almost destroyed by the
       <a href="/wiki/1692_Jamaica_earthquake" title="1692 Jamaica earthquake">
        1692 Jamaica earthquake
       </a>
       .
      </p>
      <p>
       The
       <a href="/wiki/Irish_people_in_Jamaica" title="Irish people in Jamaica">
        Irish in Jamaica
       </a>
       also formed a large part of the island's early population, making up 2 thirds of the white population on the island in the late 17th century, twice that of the English population. They were brought in as indentured labourers and soldiers after the conquest of Jamaica by Cromwells forces in 1655, The majority of Irish were transported by force as political prisoners of war from Ireland as a result of the ongoing
       <a href="/wiki/Wars_of_the_Three_Kingdoms" title="Wars of the Three Kingdoms">
        Wars of the Three Kingdoms
       </a>
       at the time.
       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-21">
        <a href="#cite_note-21">
         [21]
        </a>
       </sup>
       Migration of large numbers Irish to the island continued into the 18th century.
       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-22">
        <a href="#cite_note-22">
         [22]
        </a>
       </sup>
      </p>
      <p>
       Jews were expelled from Spain in 1492 and then forcibly converted to Christianity in Portugal, during a period of persecution by the Inquisition. Some Spanish and Portuguese Jewish refugees went to the Netherlands and England, and from there to Jamaica. Others were part of the Iberian colonisation of the New World, after overtly converting to Catholicism, as only Catholics were allowed in the Spanish colonies. By 1660, Jamaica had become a refuge for Jews in the New World, also attracting those who had been expelled from Spain and Portugal.
      </p>
      <p>
       An early group of Jews arrived in 1510, soon after the son of Christopher Columbus settled on the island. Primarily working as merchants and traders, the Jewish community was forced to live a clandestine life, calling themselves "Portugals". After the British took over rule of Jamaica, the Jews decided the best defense against Spain's regaining control was to encourage making the colony a base for Caribbean pirates. With the pirates installed in
       <a href="/wiki/Port_Royal" title="Port Royal">
        Port Royal
       </a>
       , which became the largest city in the Caribbean, the Spanish would be deterred from attacking. The British leaders agreed with the viability of this strategy to forestall outside aggression.
       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-23">
        <a href="#cite_note-23">
         [23]
        </a>
       </sup>
      </p>
      <p>
       When the English captured Jamaica in 1655, the Spanish colonists fled after freeing their slaves.
       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-jamsenghist_16-1">
        <a href="#cite_note-jamsenghist-16">
         [16]
        </a>
       </sup>
       The slaves dispersed into the mountains, joining the
       <i>
        <a href="/wiki/Maroon_(people)" title="Maroon (people)">
         maroons
        </a>
        ,
       </i>
       those who had previously escaped to live with the
       <a href="/wiki/Ta%C3%ADno" title="Taíno">
        Taíno
       </a>
       native people.
       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-maroons_24-0">
        <a href="#cite_note-maroons-24">
         [24]
        </a>
       </sup>
       During the centuries of slavery, Maroons established free communities in the mountainous interior of Jamaica, where they maintained their freedom and independence for generations. The
       <a href="/wiki/Jamaican_Maroons" title="Jamaican Maroons">
        Jamaican Maroons
       </a>
       fought the British during the 18th century. Under treaties of 1738 and 1739, the British agreed to stop trying to round them up in exchange for their leaving the colonial settlements alone, but serving if needed for military actions.
       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-maroons_24-1">
        <a href="#cite_note-maroons-24">
         [24]
        </a>
       </sup>
       Some of the communities were broken up and the British deported Maroons to
       <a href="/wiki/Nova_Scotia" title="Nova Scotia">
        Nova Scotia
       </a>
       and, later,
       <a href="/wiki/Sierra_Leone" title="Sierra Leone">
        Sierra Leone
       </a>
       . The name is still used today by modern Maroon descendants, who have certain rights and autonomy at the community of
       <a href="/wiki/Accompong" title="Accompong">
        Accompong
       </a>
       .
      </p>
      <p>
       During its first 200 years of British rule, Jamaica became one of the world's leading
       <a href="/wiki/Sugar" title="Sugar">
        sugar
       </a>
       -exporting, slave-dependent colonies, producing more than 77,000 tons of sugar annually between 1820 and 1824. After the
       <a href="/wiki/Slave_Trade_Act_1807" title="Slave Trade Act 1807">
        abolition of the international slave trade
       </a>
       in 1807,
       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-25">
        <a href="#cite_note-25">
         [25]
        </a>
       </sup>
       the British began to "import"
       <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Indentured_servant" title="Indentured servant">
        indentured servants
       </a>
       to supplement the labour pool, as many freedmen resisted working on the plantations. After slavery was abolished, workers recruited from India began arriving in 1845, Chinese workers in 1854,
       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-26">
        <a href="#cite_note-26">
         [26]
        </a>
       </sup>
       as many freedmen resisted working on the plantations. Many South Asian and Chinese descendants continue to reside in Jamaica today.
       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-27">
        <a href="#cite_note-27">
         [27]
        </a>
       </sup>
       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-28">
        <a href="#cite_note-28">
         [28]
        </a>
       </sup>
      </p>
      <div class="thumb tright">
       <div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;">
        <a class="image" href="/wiki/File:Hakewill,_A_Picturesque_Tour_of_the_Island_of_Jamaica,_Plate_19.jpg">
         <img alt="" class="thumbimage" data-file-height="1613" data-file-width="2461" height="144" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/b/bb/Hakewill%2C_A_Picturesque_Tour_of_the_Island_of_Jamaica%2C_Plate_19.jpg/220px-Hakewill%2C_A_Picturesque_Tour_of_the_Island_of_Jamaica%2C_Plate_19.jpg" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/b/bb/Hakewill%2C_A_Picturesque_Tour_of_the_Island_of_Jamaica%2C_Plate_19.jpg/330px-Hakewill%2C_A_Picturesque_Tour_of_the_Island_of_Jamaica%2C_Plate_19.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/b/bb/Hakewill%2C_A_Picturesque_Tour_of_the_Island_of_Jamaica%2C_Plate_19.jpg/440px-Hakewill%2C_A_Picturesque_Tour_of_the_Island_of_Jamaica%2C_Plate_19.jpg 2x" width="220"/>
        </a>
        <div class="thumbcaption">
         <div class="magnify">
          <a class="internal" href="/wiki/File:Hakewill,_A_Picturesque_Tour_of_the_Island_of_Jamaica,_Plate_19.jpg" title="Enlarge">
          </a>
         </div>
         Montpelier Plantation, the property of C. R. Ellis, Esq. M.P., c. 1820
        </div>
       </div>
      </div>
      <p>
       By the beginning of the 19th century, Jamaica's dependence on slave labour and a plantation economy had resulted in black people outnumbering white people by a ratio of almost 20 to 1. Although the UK had outlawed the importation of slaves, some were still smuggled in from Spanish colonies and directly. While planning the abolition of slavery, the British Parliament passed laws to improve conditions for slaves. They banned the use of whips in the field and flogging of women; informed planters that slaves were to be allowed religious instruction, and required a free day during each week when slaves could sell their produce,
       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-29">
        <a href="#cite_note-29">
         [29]
        </a>
       </sup>
       prohibiting Sunday markets to enable slaves to attend church.
       <sup class="noprint Inline-Template Template-Fact" style="white-space:nowrap;">
        [
        <i>
         <a href="/wiki/Wikipedia:Citation_needed" title="Wikipedia:Citation needed">
          <span title="This claim needs references to reliable sources. (February 2016)">
           citation needed
          </span>
         </a>
        </i>
        ]
       </sup>
      </p>
      <p>
       The House of Assembly in Jamaica resented and resisted the new laws. Members (then restricted to European-Jamaicans) claimed that the slaves were content and objected to Parliament's interference in island affairs. Slave owners feared possible revolts if conditions were lightened. Following a series of rebellions on the island and changing attitudes in Great Britain, the British government formally abolished slavery by an 1833 act, beginning in 1834, with full
       <a href="/wiki/Abolitionism_in_the_United_Kingdom" title="Abolitionism in the United Kingdom">
        emancipation
       </a>
       from chattel slavery declared in 1838. The population in 1834 was 371,070, of whom 15,000 were white, 5,000 free black; 40,000 'coloured' or
       <a href="/wiki/Free_people_of_color" title="Free people of color">
        free people of color
       </a>
       (
       <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Mixed_race" title="Mixed race">
        mixed race
       </a>
       ); and 311,070 were slaves.
       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-population_19-1">
        <a href="#cite_note-population-19">
         [19]
        </a>
       </sup>
      </p>
      <p>
       In the 19th century, the British established a number of
       <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Botanical_gardens" title="Botanical gardens">
        botanical gardens
       </a>
       . These included the
       <a class="new" href="/w/index.php?title=Castleton_Botanical_Gardens&amp;action=edit&amp;redlink=1" title="Castleton Botanical Gardens (page does not exist)">
        Castleton Botanical Gardens
       </a>
       , developed in 1862 to replace the
       <a href="/wiki/Bath,_Jamaica" title="Bath, Jamaica">
        Bath Botanical Gardens
       </a>
       (created in 1779) which was subject to flooding.
       <a href="/wiki/Bath,_Jamaica" title="Bath, Jamaica">
        Bath Botanical Gardens
       </a>
       was the site for planting
       <a href="/wiki/Breadfruit" title="Breadfruit">
        breadfruit
       </a>
       , brought to Jamaica from the Pacific by Captain
       <a href="/wiki/William_Bligh" title="William Bligh">
        William Bligh
       </a>
       . It became a staple in island diets. Other gardens were the
       <a href="/wiki/Cinchona" title="Cinchona">
        Cinchona
       </a>
       <a href="/wiki/Plantation" title="Plantation">
        Plantation
       </a>
       , founded in 1868, and the
       <a href="/wiki/Hope_Botanical_Gardens" title="Hope Botanical Gardens">
        Hope Botanical Gardens
       </a>
       founded in 1874. In 1872,
       <a href="/wiki/Kingston,_Jamaica" title="Kingston, Jamaica">
        Kingston
       </a>
       was designated as the island's capital.
      </p>
      <p>
       In 1945,
       <a href="/wiki/Horace_Hearne" title="Horace Hearne">
        Sir Horace Hector Hearne
       </a>
       became
       <a href="/wiki/Chief_Justice" title="Chief Justice">
        Chief Justice
       </a>
       and Keeper of the Records in Jamaica. He headed the
       <a href="/wiki/Supreme_court" title="Supreme court">
        Supreme Court
       </a>
       , Kingston between 1945 and 1950/1951. After
       <a href="/wiki/Kenya" title="Kenya">
        Kenya
       </a>
       achieved independence, its government appointed him as Chief Justice and he moved there.
      </p>
      <h3>
       <span id="Independence_.281962.29">
       </span>
       <span class="mw-headline" id="Independence_(1962)">
        Independence (1962)
       </span>
      </h3>
      <div class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable" role="note">
       Main article:
       <a href="/wiki/Independence_of_Jamaica" title="Independence of Jamaica">
        Independence of Jamaica
       </a>
      </div>
      <div class="thumb tright">
       <div class="thumbinner" style="width:172px;">
        <a class="image" href="/wiki/File:Charles_Camilla_Jamaica_2008.jpg">
         <img alt="" class="thumbimage" data-file-height="2525" data-file-width="1805" height="238" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/a/ae/Charles_Camilla_Jamaica_2008.jpg/170px-Charles_Camilla_Jamaica_2008.jpg" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/a/ae/Charles_Camilla_Jamaica_2008.jpg/255px-Charles_Camilla_Jamaica_2008.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/a/ae/Charles_Camilla_Jamaica_2008.jpg/340px-Charles_Camilla_Jamaica_2008.jpg 2x" width="170"/>
        </a>
        <div class="thumbcaption">
         <div class="magnify">
          <a class="internal" href="/wiki/File:Charles_Camilla_Jamaica_2008.jpg" title="Enlarge">
          </a>
         </div>
         <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Prince_Charles" title="Prince Charles">
          Prince Charles
         </a>
         and the
         <a href="/wiki/Duchess_of_Cornwall" title="Duchess of Cornwall">
          Duchess of Cornwall
         </a>
         during a visit to Jamaica in 2008
        </div>
       </div>
      </div>
      <p>
       Jamaica slowly gained increasing independence from the United Kingdom. In 1958, it became a province in the
       <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Federation_of_the_West_Indies" title="Federation of the West Indies">
        Federation of the West Indies
       </a>
       , a federation among the
       <a href="/wiki/British_West_Indies" title="British West Indies">
        British West Indies
       </a>
       . Jamaica attained full independence by leaving the federation in 1962.
      </p>
      <p>
       Strong economic growth, averaging approximately 6% per annum, marked the first ten years of independence under conservative
       <a href="/wiki/Jamaica_Labour_Party" title="Jamaica Labour Party">
        Jamaica Labour Party
       </a>
       governments; they were led successively by Prime Ministers
       <a href="/wiki/Alexander_Bustamante" title="Alexander Bustamante">
        Alexander Bustamante
       </a>
       ,
       <a href="/wiki/Donald_Sangster" title="Donald Sangster">
        Donald Sangster
       </a>
       and
       <a href="/wiki/Hugh_Shearer" title="Hugh Shearer">
        Hugh Shearer
       </a>
       . The growth was fueled by strong private investments in
       <a href="/wiki/Bauxite" title="Bauxite">
        bauxite
       </a>
       /alumina,
       <a href="/wiki/Tourism" title="Tourism">
        tourism
       </a>
       , the manufacturing industry and, to a lesser extent, the agricultural sector.
      </p>
      <p>
       The optimism of the first decade was accompanied by a growing sense of inequality among many Afro-Jamaicans, and a concern that the benefits of growth were not being shared by the urban poor.
       <sup class="noprint Inline-Template Template-Fact" style="white-space:nowrap;">
        [
        <i>
         <a href="/wiki/Wikipedia:Citation_needed" title="Wikipedia:Citation needed">
          <span title="This claim needs references to reliable sources. (March 2016)">
           citation needed
          </span>
         </a>
        </i>
        ]
       </sup>
       Combined with the effects of a slowdown in the global economy in 1970,
       <sup class="noprint Inline-Template Template-Fact" style="white-space:nowrap;">
        [
        <i>
         <a href="/wiki/Wikipedia:Citation_needed" title="Wikipedia:Citation needed">
          <span title="This claim needs references to reliable sources. (March 2016)">
           citation needed
          </span>
         </a>
        </i>
        ]
       </sup>
       the voters elected the PNP (
       <a href="/wiki/People%27s_National_Party" title="People's National Party">
        People's National Party
       </a>
       ) in 1972. They tried to implement more socially equitable policies in education and health, but the economy suffered under their leadership. By 1980, Jamaica's gross national product had declined to some 25% below the 1972 level. Due to rising foreign and local debt, accompanied by large fiscal deficits, the government sought
       <a href="/wiki/International_Monetary_Fund" title="International Monetary Fund">
        International Monetary Fund
       </a>
       (IMF) financing from the United States and others.
      </p>
      <p>
       Economic deterioration continued into the mid-1980s, exacerbated by a number of factors. The first and third largest alumina producers,
       <a href="/wiki/Alpart" title="Alpart">
        Alpart
       </a>
       and
       <a href="/wiki/Alcoa" title="Alcoa">
        Alcoa
       </a>
       , closed, and there was a significant reduction in production by the second-largest producer,
       <a href="/wiki/Alcan" title="Alcan">
        Alcan
       </a>
       . Reynolds Jamaica Mines, Ltd. left the Jamaican industry. There was also a decline in tourism, which was important to the economy.
      </p>
      <p>
       Independence, however widely celebrated in Jamaica, has been questioned in the early 21st century. In 2011, a survey showed that approximately 60% of Jamaicans believe that the country would be better off had it remained a British colony with only 17% believing it would be worse off, citing as problems years of social and fiscal mismanagement in the country.
       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-30">
        <a href="#cite_note-30">
         [30]
        </a>
       </sup>
       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-31">
        <a href="#cite_note-31">
         [31]
        </a>
       </sup>
      </p>
      <h2>
       <span class="mw-headline" id="Government_and_politics">
        Government and politics
       </span>
      </h2>
      <div class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable" role="note">
       Main article:
       <a href="/wiki/Politics_of_Jamaica" title="Politics of Jamaica">
        Politics of Jamaica
       </a>
      </div>
      <div class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable" role="note">
       Further information:
       <a href="/wiki/Foreign_relations_of_Jamaica" title="Foreign relations of Jamaica">
        Foreign relations of Jamaica
       </a>
       and
       <a href="/wiki/Republicanism_in_Jamaica" title="Republicanism in Jamaica">
        Republicanism in Jamaica
       </a>
      </div>
      <div class="thumb tright">
       <div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;">
        <a class="image" href="/wiki/File:Parliament.jm.jpg">
         <img alt="" class="thumbimage" data-file-height="336" data-file-width="448" height="165" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/f/f7/Parliament.jm.jpg/220px-Parliament.jm.jpg" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/f/f7/Parliament.jm.jpg/330px-Parliament.jm.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/f/f7/Parliament.jm.jpg/440px-Parliament.jm.jpg 2x" width="220"/>
        </a>
        <div class="thumbcaption">
         <div class="magnify">
          <a class="internal" href="/wiki/File:Parliament.jm.jpg" title="Enlarge">
          </a>
         </div>
         Inside the
         <a href="/wiki/Parliament_of_Jamaica" title="Parliament of Jamaica">
          Jamaican Parliament
         </a>
        </div>
       </div>
      </div>
      <p>
       Jamaica is a
       <a href="/wiki/Parliamentary_system" title="Parliamentary system">
        parliamentary democracy
       </a>
       and
       <a href="/wiki/Constitutional_monarchy" title="Constitutional monarchy">
        constitutional monarchy
       </a>
       , with
       <a href="/wiki/Elizabeth_II" title="Elizabeth II">
        Queen Elizabeth II
       </a>
       serving as the
       <a href="/wiki/Monarchy_of_Jamaica" title="Monarchy of Jamaica">
        Jamaican monarch
       </a>
       .
       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-32">
        <a href="#cite_note-32">
         [32]
        </a>
       </sup>
       As Elizabeth II is shared as
       <a href="/wiki/Head_of_state" title="Head of state">
        head of state
       </a>
       of
       <a href="/wiki/Commonwealth_realm" title="Commonwealth realm">
        fifteen other countries
       </a>
       and resides mostly in the United Kingdom, she is thus often represented as Queen of Jamaica in Jamaica and abroad by the
       <a href="/wiki/Governor-General_of_Jamaica" title="Governor-General of Jamaica">
        Governor-General of Jamaica
       </a>
       .
       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-33">
        <a href="#cite_note-33">
         [33]
        </a>
       </sup>
      </p>
      <p>
       The governor-general is nominated by the
       <a href="/wiki/Prime_Minister_of_Jamaica" title="Prime Minister of Jamaica">
        Prime Minister of Jamaica
       </a>
       and the entire Cabinet and appointed by the monarch. All the members of the Cabinet are appointed by the governor-general on the advice of the prime minister. The monarch and the governor-general serve largely ceremonial roles, apart from their
       <a href="/wiki/Reserve_power" title="Reserve power">
        reserve powers
       </a>
       for use in certain constitutional crisis situations.
      </p>
      <p>
       Jamaica's current
       <a href="/wiki/Constitution" title="Constitution">
        constitution
       </a>
       was drafted in 1962 by a bipartisan joint committee of the Jamaican legislature. It came into force with the Jamaica Independence Act, 1962 of the
       <a href="/wiki/Parliament_of_the_United_Kingdom" title="Parliament of the United Kingdom">
        United Kingdom parliament
       </a>
       , which gave Jamaica independence.
      </p>
      <p>
       The
       <a href="/wiki/Parliament_of_Jamaica" title="Parliament of Jamaica">
        Parliament of Jamaica
       </a>
       is
       <a href="/wiki/Bicameralism" title="Bicameralism">
        bicameral
       </a>
       , consisting of the House of Representatives (Lower House) and the Senate (Upper House). Members of the House (known as Members of Parliament or
       <i>
        MPs
       </i>
       ) are directly elected, and the member of the House of Representatives who, in the governor-general's best judgement, is best able to command the confidence of a majority of the members of that House, is appointed by the governor-general to be the prime minister. Senators are nominated jointly by the prime minister and the parliamentary
       <a href="/wiki/Opposition_(parliamentary)" title="Opposition (parliamentary)">
        Leader of the Opposition
       </a>
       and are then appointed by the governor-general.
      </p>
      <h3>
       <span class="mw-headline" id="Political_culture">
        Political culture
       </span>
      </h3>
      <p>
       Jamaica has traditionally had a
       <a href="/wiki/Two-party_system" title="Two-party system">
        two-party system
       </a>
       , with power often alternating between the
       <a href="/wiki/People%27s_National_Party" title="People's National Party">
        People's National Party
       </a>
       (PNP) and
       <a href="/wiki/Jamaica_Labour_Party" title="Jamaica Labour Party">
        Jamaica Labour Party
       </a>
       (JLP). The party with current administrative and legislative power is the Jamaica Labour Party, with a one-seat parliamentary majority as of 2016
       <sup class="plainlinks noexcerpt noprint asof-tag update" style="display:none;">
        <a class="external text" href="//en.wikipedia.org/w/index.php?title=Jamaica&amp;action=edit">
         [update]
        </a>
       </sup>
       . There are also several minor parties who have yet to gain a seat in parliament; the largest of these is the
       <a href="/wiki/National_Democratic_Movement_(Jamaica)" title="National Democratic Movement (Jamaica)">
        National Democratic Movement
       </a>
       (NDM).
      </p>
      <h3>
       <span class="mw-headline" id="Administrative_divisions">
        Administrative divisions
       </span>
      </h3>
      <div class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable" role="note">
       Main article:
       <a href="/wiki/Parishes_of_Jamaica" title="Parishes of Jamaica">
        Parishes of Jamaica
       </a>
      </div>
      <p>
       Jamaica is divided into 14
       <a href="/wiki/Parishes_of_Jamaica" title="Parishes of Jamaica">
        parishes
       </a>
       , which are grouped into three historic
       <a href="/wiki/County" title="County">
        counties
       </a>
       that have no administrative relevance.
      </p>
      <p>
       In the context of
       <a href="/wiki/Local_government" title="Local government">
        local government
       </a>
       the parishes are designated "Local Authorities." These local authorities are further styled as "Municipal Corporations," which are either city municipalities or town municipalities.
       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-localgovernemtn_34-0">
        <a href="#cite_note-localgovernemtn-34">
         [34]
        </a>
       </sup>
       Any new city municipality must have a population of at least 50,000, and a town municipality a number set by the Minister of Local Government.
       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-localgovernemtn_34-1">
        <a href="#cite_note-localgovernemtn-34">
         [34]
        </a>
       </sup>
       There are currently no town municipalities.
      </p>
      <p>
       The local governments of the parishes of Kingston and St. Andrews are consolidated as the city municipality of Kingston &amp; St. Andrew Municipal Corporation. The newest city municipality created is the Municipality of Portmore in 2003. While it is geographically located within the parish of St. Catherine, it is governed independently.
      </p>

       <div class="floatnone">
        <div class="noresize" style="height: 159px; width: 400px; ">
         <map name="ImageMap_1_473781842">
