      </div>
      <h3>
       <span class="mw-headline" id="Military">
        Military
       </span>
      </h3>
      <div class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable" role="note">
       Main article:
       <a href="/wiki/Jamaica_Defence_Force" title="Jamaica Defence Force">
        Jamaica Defence Force
       </a>
      </div>
      <div class="thumb tright">
       <div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;">
        <a class="image" href="/wiki/File:FN_FAL_DA-SD-04-01067.jpg">
         <img alt="" class="thumbimage" data-file-height="3000" data-file-width="1955" height="338" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/e/e9/FN_FAL_DA-SD-04-01067.jpg/220px-FN_FAL_DA-SD-04-01067.jpg" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/e/e9/FN_FAL_DA-SD-04-01067.jpg/330px-FN_FAL_DA-SD-04-01067.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/e/e9/FN_FAL_DA-SD-04-01067.jpg/440px-FN_FAL_DA-SD-04-01067.jpg 2x" width="220"/>
        </a>
        <div class="thumbcaption">
         <div class="magnify">
          <a class="internal" href="/wiki/File:FN_FAL_DA-SD-04-01067.jpg" title="Enlarge">
          </a>
         </div>
         Jamaican soldiers training to fire the
         <a href="/wiki/FN_FAL" title="FN FAL">
          FN FAL
         </a>
         in 2002
        </div>
       </div>
      </div>
      <p>
       The Jamaica Defence Force (JDF) is the small but professional military force of Jamaica. The JDF is based on the British military model with similar organisation, training, weapons and traditions. Once chosen, officer candidates are sent to one of several British or Canadian basic officer courses depending on the arm of service. Enlisted soldiers are given basic training at Up Park Camp or JDF Training Depot, Newcastle, both in St. Andrew. As with the British model, NCOs are given several levels of professional training as they rise up the ranks. Additional military schools are available for speciality training in Canada, the United States and the United Kingdom.
      </p>
      <p>
       The JDF is directly descended from the British Army's
       <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/West_India_Regiment" title="West India Regiment">
        West India Regiment
       </a>
       formed during the colonial era.
       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-jdfhistory_35-0">
        <a href="#cite_note-jdfhistory-35">
         [35]
        </a>
       </sup>
       The West India Regiment was used extensively by the British Empire in policing the empire from 1795 to 1926. Other units in the JDF heritage include the early colonial Jamaica Militia, the Kingston Infantry Volunteers of WWI and reorganised into the Jamaican Infantry Volunteers in World War II. The West Indies Regiment was reformed in 1958 as part of the
       <a href="/wiki/West_Indies_Federation" title="West Indies Federation">
        West Indies Federation
       </a>
       , after dissolution of the Federation the JDF was established.
      </p>
      <p>
       The Jamaica Defence Force (JDF) comprises an
       <a href="/wiki/The_Jamaica_Regiment" title="The Jamaica Regiment">
        infantry Regiment
       </a>
       and Reserve Corps, an Air Wing, a Coast Guard fleet and a supporting Engineering Unit.
       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-JDFstructure_36-0">
        <a href="#cite_note-JDFstructure-36">
         [36]
        </a>
       </sup>
       The infantry regiment contains the 1st, 2nd and 3rd (National Reserve) battalions. The JDF Air Wing is divided into three flight units, a training unit, a support unit and the JDF Air Wing (National Reserve). The Coast Guard is divided between seagoing crews and support crews who conduct maritime safety and maritime law enforcement as well as defence-related operations.
       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-cgroles_37-0">
        <a href="#cite_note-cgroles-37">
         [37]
        </a>
       </sup>
      </p>
      <p>
       The role of the support battalion is to provide support to boost numbers in combat and issue competency training in order to allow for the readiness of the force.
       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-csbattalion_38-0">
        <a href="#cite_note-csbattalion-38">
         [38]
        </a>
       </sup>
       The 1st Engineer Regiment was formed due to an increased demand for military engineers and their role is to provide engineering services whenever and wherever they are needed.
       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-engineerhistory_39-0">
        <a href="#cite_note-engineerhistory-39">
         [39]
        </a>
       </sup>
       The Headquarters JDF contains the JDF Commander, Command Staff as well as Intelligence, Judge Advocate office, Administrative and Procurement sections.
       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-jdfhq_40-0">
        <a href="#cite_note-jdfhq-40">
         [40]
        </a>
       </sup>
      </p>
      <p>
       In recent years the JDF has been called on to assist the nation's police, the
       <a href="/wiki/Jamaica_Constabulary_Force" title="Jamaica Constabulary Force">
        Jamaica Constabulary Force
       </a>
       (JCF), in fighting drug smuggling and a rising crime rate which includes one of the highest murder rates in the world. JDF units actively conduct armed patrols with the JCF in high-crime areas and known gang neighbourhoods. There has been vocal controversy as well as support of this JDF role. In early 2005, an Opposition leader,
       <a href="/wiki/Edward_Seaga" title="Edward Seaga">
        Edward Seaga
       </a>
       , called for the merger of the JDF and JCF. This has not garnered support in either organisation nor among the majority of citizens.
      </p>
      <h2>
       <span class="mw-headline" id="Geography_and_environment">
        Geography and environment
       </span>
      </h2>
      <div class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable" role="note">
       Main article:
       <a href="/wiki/Geography_of_Jamaica" title="Geography of Jamaica">
        Geography of Jamaica
       </a>
      </div>
      <div class="thumb tright">
       <div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;">
        <a class="image" href="/wiki/File:Doctors-Cave-Beach.jpg">
         <img alt="" class="thumbimage" data-file-height="529" data-file-width="1011" height="115" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/a/ac/Doctors-Cave-Beach.jpg/220px-Doctors-Cave-Beach.jpg" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/a/ac/Doctors-Cave-Beach.jpg/330px-Doctors-Cave-Beach.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/a/ac/Doctors-Cave-Beach.jpg/440px-Doctors-Cave-Beach.jpg 2x" width="220"/>
        </a>
        <div class="thumbcaption">
         <div class="magnify">
          <a class="internal" href="/wiki/File:Doctors-Cave-Beach.jpg" title="Enlarge">
          </a>
         </div>
         <a href="/wiki/Doctor%27s_Cave_Beach_Club" title="Doctor's Cave Beach Club">
          Doctor's Cave Beach Club
         </a>
         is a popular destination in
         <a href="/wiki/Montego_Bay" title="Montego Bay">
          Montego Bay
         </a>
         .
        </div>
       </div>
      </div>
      <div class="thumb tright">
       <div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;">
        <a class="image" href="/wiki/File:Dunns_River_Falls_Photo_D_Ramey_Logan.jpg">
         <img alt="" class="thumbimage" data-file-height="2848" data-file-width="4288" height="146" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/6/63/Dunns_River_Falls_Photo_D_Ramey_Logan.jpg/220px-Dunns_River_Falls_Photo_D_Ramey_Logan.jpg" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/6/63/Dunns_River_Falls_Photo_D_Ramey_Logan.jpg/330px-Dunns_River_Falls_Photo_D_Ramey_Logan.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/6/63/Dunns_River_Falls_Photo_D_Ramey_Logan.jpg/440px-Dunns_River_Falls_Photo_D_Ramey_Logan.jpg 2x" width="220"/>
        </a>
        <div class="thumbcaption">
         <div class="magnify">
          <a class="internal" href="/wiki/File:Dunns_River_Falls_Photo_D_Ramey_Logan.jpg" title="Enlarge">
          </a>
         </div>
         The picturesque
         <a href="/wiki/Dunn%27s_River_Falls" title="Dunn's River Falls">
          Dunn's River Falls
         </a>
         in
         <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Ocho_R%C3%ADos" title="Ocho Ríos">
          Ocho Ríos
         </a>
        </div>
       </div>
      </div>
      <p>
       Jamaica is the third largest island in the
       <a href="/wiki/Caribbean" title="Caribbean">
        Caribbean
       </a>
       .
       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-jamaica_background_41-0">
        <a href="#cite_note-jamaica_background-41">
         [41]
        </a>
       </sup>
       It lies between latitudes
       <a href="/wiki/17th_parallel_north" title="17th parallel north">
        17°
       </a>
       and
       <a href="/wiki/19th_parallel_north" title="19th parallel north">
        19°N
       </a>
       , and longitudes
       <a href="/wiki/76th_meridian_west" title="76th meridian west">
        76°
       </a>
       and
       <a href="/wiki/79th_meridian_west" title="79th meridian west">
        79°W
       </a>
       . Mountains, including the
       <a href="/wiki/Blue_Mountains_(Jamaica)" title="Blue Mountains (Jamaica)">
        Blue Mountains
       </a>
       , dominate the inland. They are surrounded by a narrow coastal plain.
       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Geogofjam_42-0">
        <a href="#cite_note-Geogofjam-42">
         [42]
        </a>
       </sup>
       Jamaica only has two cities, the first being
       <a href="/wiki/Kingston,_Jamaica" title="Kingston, Jamaica">
        Kingston
       </a>
       , the capital city and centre of business, located on the south coast and the 'second' city being
       <a href="/wiki/Montego_Bay" title="Montego Bay">
        Montego Bay
       </a>
       , one of the best known cities in the
       <a href="/wiki/Caribbean" title="Caribbean">
        Caribbean
       </a>
       for
       <a href="/wiki/Tourism" title="Tourism">
        tourism
       </a>
       , located on the north coast. Other towns include
       <a href="/wiki/Portmore,_Jamaica" title="Portmore, Jamaica">
        Portmore
       </a>
       ,
       <a href="/wiki/Spanish_Town" title="Spanish Town">
        Spanish Town
       </a>
       ,
       <a href="/wiki/Mandeville,_Jamaica" title="Mandeville, Jamaica">
        Mandeville
       </a>
       and the resort towns of
       <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Ocho_R%C3%ADos" title="Ocho Ríos">
        Ocho Ríos
       </a>
       ,
       <a href="/wiki/Port_Antonio" title="Port Antonio">
        Port Antonio
       </a>
       and
       <a href="/wiki/Negril" title="Negril">
        Negril
       </a>
       .
       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-majortownsandcities_43-0">
        <a href="#cite_note-majortownsandcities-43">
         [43]
        </a>
       </sup>
      </p>
      <p>
       <a href="/wiki/Kingston_Harbour" title="Kingston Harbour">
        Kingston Harbour
       </a>
       is the seventh-largest natural harbour in the world,
       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-portauthority_44-0">
        <a href="#cite_note-portauthority-44">
         [44]
        </a>
       </sup>
       which contributed to the city being designated as the capital in 1872.
      </p>
      <p>
       Tourist attractions include
       <a href="/wiki/Dunn%27s_River_Falls" title="Dunn's River Falls">
        Dunn's River Falls
       </a>
       in St. Ann, YS Falls in St. Elizabeth, the Blue Lagoon in
       <a href="/wiki/Portland_Parish" title="Portland Parish">
        Portland
       </a>
       , believed to be the crater of an extinct volcano.
       <a href="/wiki/Port_Royal" title="Port Royal">
        Port Royal
       </a>
       was the site of
       <a href="/wiki/1692_Jamaica_earthquake" title="1692 Jamaica earthquake">
        a major earthquake in 1692
       </a>
       that helped form the island's
       <a href="/wiki/Palisadoes" title="Palisadoes">
        Palisadoes
       </a>
       .
       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-kingston_45-0">
        <a href="#cite_note-kingston-45">
         [45]
        </a>
       </sup>
       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-jamtourist_46-0">
        <a href="#cite_note-jamtourist-46">
         [46]
        </a>
       </sup>
       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-portantonio_47-0">
        <a href="#cite_note-portantonio-47">
         [47]
        </a>
       </sup>
       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-ochorios_48-0">
        <a href="#cite_note-ochorios-48">
         [48]
        </a>
       </sup>
      </p>
      <p>
       The climate in Jamaica is tropical, with hot and humid weather, although higher inland regions are more temperate.
       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-climate_49-0">
        <a href="#cite_note-climate-49">
         [49]
        </a>
       </sup>
       Some regions on the south coast, such as the Liguanea Plain and the Pedro Plains, are relatively dry
       <a href="/wiki/Rain_shadow" title="Rain shadow">
        rain-shadow
       </a>
       areas.
       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Gleaner_Climate_50-0">
        <a href="#cite_note-Gleaner_Climate-50">
         [50]
        </a>
       </sup>
      </p>
      <p>
       Jamaica lies in the
       <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Hurricane_belt" title="Hurricane belt">
        hurricane belt
       </a>
       of the
       <a href="/wiki/Atlantic_Ocean" title="Atlantic Ocean">
        Atlantic Ocean
       </a>
       and because of this, the island sometimes suffers significant storm damage.
       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-jamhurricanes_51-0">
        <a href="#cite_note-jamhurricanes-51">
         [51]
        </a>
       </sup>
       Hurricanes
       <a href="/wiki/Hurricane_Charlie_(1951)" title="Hurricane Charlie (1951)">
        Charlie
       </a>
       and
       <a href="/wiki/Hurricane_Gilbert" title="Hurricane Gilbert">
        Gilbert
       </a>
       hit Jamaica directly in 1951 and 1988, respectively, causing major damage and many deaths. In the 2000s (decade), hurricanes
       <a href="/wiki/Hurricane_Ivan" title="Hurricane Ivan">
        Ivan
       </a>
       ,
       <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Hurricane_Dean_(2007)" title="Hurricane Dean (2007)">
        Dean
       </a>
       , and
       <a href="/wiki/Hurricane_Gustav" title="Hurricane Gustav">
        Gustav
       </a>
       also brought severe weather to the island.
      </p>
      <p>
       Among the variety of terrestrial, aquatic and marine ecosystems are dry and wet limestone forests, rainforest, riparian woodland, wetlands, caves, rivers, seagrass beds and coral reefs. The authorities have recognised the tremendous significance and potential of the environment and have designated some of the more 'fertile' areas as 'protected'. Among the island's protected areas are the
       <a href="/wiki/Cockpit_Country" title="Cockpit Country">
        Cockpit Country
       </a>
       ,
       <a href="/wiki/Jamaican_dry_forests" title="Jamaican dry forests">
        Hellshire Hills
       </a>
       , and Litchfield forest reserves. In 1992, Jamaica's first marine park, covering nearly 15 square kilometres (5.8 sq mi), was established in
       <a href="/wiki/Montego_Bay" title="Montego Bay">
        Montego Bay
       </a>
       .
       <a href="/wiki/Portland_Bight_Protected_Area" title="Portland Bight Protected Area">
        Portland Bight Protected Area
       </a>
       was designated in 1999.
       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-52">
        <a href="#cite_note-52">
         [52]
        </a>
       </sup>
      </p>
      <p>
       The following year
       <a href="/wiki/Blue_and_John_Crow_Mountains_National_Park" title="Blue and John Crow Mountains National Park">
        Blue and John Crow Mountains National Park
       </a>
       was created on roughly 300 square miles (780 km
       <sup>
        2
       </sup>
       ) of wilderness, which supports thousands of tree and fern species and rare animals.
      </p>
      <h3>
       <span class="mw-headline" id="Flora_and_fauna">
        Flora and fauna
       </span>
      </h3>
      <div class="thumb tright">
       <div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;">
        <a class="image" href="/wiki/File:Epicrates_subflavus.jpg">
         <img alt="" class="thumbimage" data-file-height="2376" data-file-width="4224" height="124" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/d/d2/Epicrates_subflavus.jpg/220px-Epicrates_subflavus.jpg" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/d/d2/Epicrates_subflavus.jpg/330px-Epicrates_subflavus.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/d/d2/Epicrates_subflavus.jpg/440px-Epicrates_subflavus.jpg 2x" width="220"/>
        </a>
        <div class="thumbcaption">
         <div class="magnify">
          <a class="internal" href="/wiki/File:Epicrates_subflavus.jpg" title="Enlarge">
          </a>
         </div>
         <a href="/wiki/Jamaican_boa" title="Jamaican boa">
          Jamaican boa
         </a>
        </div>
       </div>
      </div>
      <div class="thumb tright">
       <div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;">
        <a class="image" href="/wiki/File:Geocapromys_brownii_Harvard_University_small.jpg">
         <img alt="" class="thumbimage" data-file-height="261" data-file-width="375" height="153" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/3/39/Geocapromys_brownii_Harvard_University_small.jpg/220px-Geocapromys_brownii_Harvard_University_small.jpg" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/3/39/Geocapromys_brownii_Harvard_University_small.jpg/330px-Geocapromys_brownii_Harvard_University_small.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/3/39/Geocapromys_brownii_Harvard_University_small.jpg 2x" width="220"/>
        </a>
        <div class="thumbcaption">
         <div class="magnify">
          <a class="internal" href="/wiki/File:Geocapromys_brownii_Harvard_University_small.jpg" title="Enlarge">
          </a>
         </div>
         <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Jamaican_hutia" title="Jamaican hutia">
          Jamaican hutia
         </a>
        </div>
       </div>
      </div>
      <p>
       Jamaica's climate is tropical, supporting diverse ecosystems with a wealth of plants and animals.
      </p>
      <p>
       Jamaica's plant life has changed considerably over the centuries. When the Spanish arrived in 1494, except for small agricultural clearings, the country was deeply forested. The European settlers cut down the great timber trees for building and ships' supplies, and cleared the plains, savannas, and mountain slopes for intense agricultural cultivation. Many new plants were introduced including sugarcane, bananas, and citrus trees.
      </p>
      <p>
       Areas of heavy rainfall contain stands of bamboo, ferns, ebony, mahogany, and rosewood. Cactus and similar dry-area plants are found along the south and southwest coastal area. Parts of the west and southwest consist of large grasslands, with scattered stands of trees.
      </p>
      <p>
       The Jamaican animal life, typical of the
       <a href="/wiki/Caribbean" title="Caribbean">
        Caribbean
       </a>
       , includes highly diversified wildlife with many endemic species found nowhere else on earth. As with other oceanic islands, land mammals are mostly
       <a href="/wiki/Bat" title="Bat">
        bats
       </a>
       . The only non-bat native mammal extant in Jamaica is the
       <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Jamaican_hutia" title="Jamaican hutia">
        Jamaican hutia
       </a>
       , locally known as the coney. Introduced mammals such as
       <a href="/wiki/Wild_boar" title="Wild boar">
        wild boar
       </a>
       and the
       <a href="/wiki/Small_Asian_mongoose" title="Small Asian mongoose">
        small Asian mongoose
       </a>
       are also common. Jamaica is also home to about 50 species of reptiles,
       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-53">
        <a href="#cite_note-53">
         [53]
        </a>
       </sup>
       the largest of which is the
       <a href="/wiki/American_crocodile" title="American crocodile">
        American crocodile
       </a>
       ; however, it is only present within the Black River and a few other areas. Lizards such as
       <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Anole" title="Anole">
        anoles
       </a>
       ,
       <a href="/wiki/Iguana" title="Iguana">
        iguanas
       </a>
       and snakes such as racers and the
       <a href="/wiki/Jamaican_boa" title="Jamaican boa">
        Jamaican boa
       </a>
       (the largest snake on the island), are common in areas such as the Cockpit Country. None of Jamaica's eight species of native snakes is venomous.
       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-54">
        <a href="#cite_note-54">
         [54]
        </a>
       </sup>
      </p>
      <p>
       One species of freshwater turtle is native to Jamaica, the
       <a href="/wiki/Jamaican_slider" title="Jamaican slider">
        Jamaican slider
       </a>
       . It is found only on Jamaica,
       <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Cat_Island_(Bahamas)" title="Cat Island (Bahamas)">
        Cat Island
       </a>
       , and a few other islands in
       <a href="/wiki/The_Bahamas" title="The Bahamas">
        the Bahamas
       </a>
       . In addition, many types of frogs are common on the island, especially
       <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Treefrog" title="Treefrog">
        treefrogs
       </a>
       . Birds are abundant, and make up the bulk of the endemic and native vertebrate species. Beautiful and exotic birds, such as the
       <a href="/wiki/Jamaican_tody" title="Jamaican tody">
        Jamaican tody
       </a>
       and the
       <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Doctor_bird" title="Doctor bird">
        doctor bird
       </a>
       (the national bird), can be found among a large number of others.
      </p>
      <p>
       Jamaican waters contain considerable resources of fresh-and saltwater fish.
       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-55">
        <a href="#cite_note-55">
         [55]
        </a>
       </sup>
       The chief varieties of saltwater fish are
       <a href="/wiki/King_mackerel" title="King mackerel">
        kingfish
       </a>
       ,
       <a href="/wiki/Carangidae" title="Carangidae">
        jack
       </a>
       ,
       <a href="/wiki/Mackerel" title="Mackerel">
        mackerel
       </a>
       ,
       <a href="/wiki/Whiting_(fish)" title="Whiting (fish)">
        whiting
       </a>
       ,
       <a href="/wiki/Bonito" title="Bonito">
        bonito
       </a>
       , and
       <a href="/wiki/Tuna" title="Tuna">
        tuna
       </a>
       . Fish that occasionally enter freshwater and estuarine environments include
       <a href="/wiki/Centropomidae" title="Centropomidae">
        snook
       </a>
       ,
       <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Epinephelus_itajara" title="Epinephelus itajara">
        jewfish
       </a>
       ,
       <a href="/wiki/Mangrove_snapper" title="Mangrove snapper">
        mangrove snapper
       </a>
       , and
       <a href="/wiki/Mullet_(fish)" title="Mullet (fish)">
        mullets
       </a>
       . Fish that spend the majority of their lives in Jamaica's fresh waters include many species of
       <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Livebearer" title="Livebearer">
        livebearers
       </a>
       ,
       <a href="/wiki/Killifish" title="Killifish">
        killifish
       </a>
       , freshwater
       <a href="/wiki/Goby" title="Goby">
        gobies
       </a>
       , the mountain mullet, and the
       <a href="/wiki/American_eel" title="American eel">
        American eel
       </a>
       .
       <a href="/wiki/Tilapia" title="Tilapia">
        Tilapia
       </a>
       have been introduced from Africa for aquaculture, and are very common.
      </p>
      <p>
       Insects and other invertebrates are abundant, including the world's largest centipede, the
       <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Amazonian_giant_centipede" title="Amazonian giant centipede">
        Amazonian giant centipede
       </a>
       , and the
       <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Homerus_swallowtail" title="Homerus swallowtail">
        Homerus swallowtail
       </a>
       , the western hemisphere's largest butterfly.
      </p>
      <h2>
       <span class="mw-headline" id="Demographics">
        Demographics
       </span>
      </h2>
      <div class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable" role="note">
       Further information:
       <a href="/wiki/Demographics_of_Jamaica" title="Demographics of Jamaica">
        Demographics of Jamaica
       </a>
       and
       <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Jamaican_people" title="Jamaican people">
        Jamaican people
       </a>
      </div>
      <h3>
       <span class="mw-headline" id="Ethnic_origins">
        Ethnic origins
       </span>
      </h3>
      <div class="thumb tright">
       <div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;">
        <a class="image" href="/wiki/File:Jamaica-demography.png">
         <img alt="" class="thumbimage" data-file-height="426" data-file-width="725" height="129" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/4/43/Jamaica-demography.png/220px-Jamaica-demography.png" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/4/43/Jamaica-demography.png/330px-Jamaica-demography.png 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/4/43/Jamaica-demography.png/440px-Jamaica-demography.png 2x" width="220"/>
        </a>
        <div class="thumbcaption">
         <div class="magnify">
          <a class="internal" href="/wiki/File:Jamaica-demography.png" title="Enlarge">
          </a>
         </div>
         Jamaica's population, 1961–2003
        </div>
       </div>
      </div>
      <div class="thumb tright">
       <div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;">
        <a class="image" href="/wiki/File:Street_in_Montigo_Bay_Jamaica_Photo_D_Ramey_Logan.jpg">
         <img alt="" class="thumbimage" data-file-height="2736" data-file-width="3648" height="165" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/3/34/Street_in_Montigo_Bay_Jamaica_Photo_D_Ramey_Logan.jpg/220px-Street_in_Montigo_Bay_Jamaica_Photo_D_Ramey_Logan.jpg" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/3/34/Street_in_Montigo_Bay_Jamaica_Photo_D_Ramey_Logan.jpg/330px-Street_in_Montigo_Bay_Jamaica_Photo_D_Ramey_Logan.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/3/34/Street_in_Montigo_Bay_Jamaica_Photo_D_Ramey_Logan.jpg/440px-Street_in_Montigo_Bay_Jamaica_Photo_D_Ramey_Logan.jpg 2x" width="220"/>
        </a>
        <div class="thumbcaption">
         <div class="magnify">
          <a class="internal" href="/wiki/File:Street_in_Montigo_Bay_Jamaica_Photo_D_Ramey_Logan.jpg" title="Enlarge">
          </a>
         </div>
         The streets of
         <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Montego_Bay,_Jamaica" title="Montego Bay, Jamaica">
          Montego Bay, Jamaica
         </a>
        </div>
       </div>
      </div>
      <p>
       According to
       <i>
        <a href="/wiki/The_World_Factbook" title="The World Factbook">
         The World Factbook
        </a>
       </i>
       , as of 2011, the majority of Jamaicans were
       <a href="/wiki/Black_people" title="Black people">
        black
       </a>
       .
       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-cia.gov_56-0">
        <a href="#cite_note-cia.gov-56">
         [56]
        </a>
       </sup>
      </p>
      <table class="wikitable sortable">
       <tr>
        <th>
         Ethnic Group
        </th>
        <th>
         %
        </th>
       </tr>
       <tr>
        <td>
         <b>
          <a href="/wiki/Afro-Jamaican" title="Afro-Jamaican">
           Black
          </a>
         </b>
         <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-WorldFactbook_1-1">
          <a href="#cite_note-WorldFactbook-1">
           [1]
          </a>
         </sup>
        </td>
        <td>
         92.1%
        </td>
       </tr>
       <tr>
        <td>
         <b>
          Mixed
         </b>
         <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-WorldFactbook_1-2">
          <a href="#cite_note-WorldFactbook-1">
           [1]
          </a>
         </sup>
        </td>
        <td>
         6.1%
        </td>
       </tr>
       <tr>
        <td>
         <b>
          Asian
         </b>
         <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-WorldFactbook_1-3">
          <a href="#cite_note-WorldFactbook-1">
           [1]
          </a>
         </sup>
        </td>
        <td>
         0.8%
        </td>
       </tr>
       <tr>
        <td>
         <b>
          Other
         </b>
         <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-WorldFactbook_1-4">
          <a href="#cite_note-WorldFactbook-1">
           [1]
          </a>
         </sup>
        </td>
        <td>
         0.4%
        </td>
       </tr>
       <tr>
        <td>
         <b>
          Unspecified
         </b>
         <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-WorldFactbook_1-5">
          <a href="#cite_note-WorldFactbook-1">
           [1]
          </a>
         </sup>
        </td>
        <td>
         0.7%
        </td>
       </tr>
      </table>
      <p>
       Much of Jamaica's black population are of African or partially African descent with many being able to trace their origins to West Africa,
       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-57">
        <a href="#cite_note-57">
         [57]
        </a>
       </sup>
       as well as Europe
       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-58">
        <a href="#cite_note-58">
         [58]
        </a>
       </sup>
       and Asia.
       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Davis2004_59-0">
        <a href="#cite_note-Davis2004-59">
         [59]
        </a>
       </sup>
       Like many other anglophone Caribbean countries, many Jamaicans with mixed ancestry self-report as
       <i>
        black
       </i>
       .
       <sup class="noprint Inline-Template Template-Fact" style="white-space:nowrap;">
        [
        <i>
         <a href="/wiki/Wikipedia:Citation_needed" title="Wikipedia:Citation needed">
          <span title="This claim needs references to reliable sources. (August 2015)">
           citation needed
          </span>
         </a>
        </i>
        ]
       </sup>
      </p>
      <p>
       Asians form the second largest group and include
       <a href="/wiki/Indo-Jamaicans" title="Indo-Jamaicans">
        Indo-Jamaicans
       </a>
       and
       <a href="/wiki/Chinese_Jamaicans" title="Chinese Jamaicans">
        Chinese Jamaicans
       </a>
       .
       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-cia.gov_56-1">
        <a href="#cite_note-cia.gov-56">
         [56]
        </a>
       </sup>
       Most are descended from indentured workers brought by the British colonial government to fill labour shortages following the abolition of slavery in 1838.
      </p>
      <p>
       In recent years, immigration has increased, coming mainly from China,
       <a href="/wiki/Haiti" title="Haiti">
        Haiti
       </a>
       ,
       <a href="/wiki/Cuba" title="Cuba">
        Cuba
       </a>
       ,
       <a href="/wiki/Colombia" title="Colombia">
        Colombia
       </a>
       , and
       <a href="/wiki/Latin_America" title="Latin America">
        Latin America
       </a>
       ; 20,000
       <a href="/wiki/Latin_Americans" title="Latin Americans">
        Latin Americans
       </a>
       reside in Jamaica.
       <sup class="noprint Inline-Template Template-Fact" style="white-space:nowrap;">
        [
        <i>
         <a href="/wiki/Wikipedia:Citation_needed" title="Wikipedia:Citation needed">
          <span title="This claim needs references to reliable sources. (October 2014)">
           citation needed
          </span>
         </a>
        </i>
        ]
       </sup>
       About 7,000
       <a href="/wiki/United_States" title="United States">
        Americans
       </a>
       also reside in Jamaica,
       <sup class="noprint Inline-Template Template-Fact" style="white-space:nowrap;">
        [
        <i>
         <a href="/wiki/Wikipedia:Citation_needed" title="Wikipedia:Citation needed">
          <span title="This claim needs references to reliable sources. (October 2014)">
           citation needed
          </span>
         </a>
        </i>
        ]
       </sup>
       as well as many first-generation American, British and
       <a href="/wiki/Canadians" title="Canadians">
        Canadians
       </a>
       of Jamaican descent.
       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-60">
        <a href="#cite_note-60">
         [60]
        </a>
       </sup>
      </p>
      <p>
       A study found that the average admixture on the island was 78.3% Sub-Saharan African, 16.0%
       <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/White_Jamaican" title="White Jamaican">
        European
       </a>
       , and 5.7% East Asian.
       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-autogenerated1_61-0">
        <a href="#cite_note-autogenerated1-61">
         [61]
        </a>
       </sup>
      </p>
      <h3>
       <span class="mw-headline" id="Languages">
        Languages
       </span>
      </h3>
      <div class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable" role="note">
       Main articles:
       <a href="/wiki/Jamaican_Patois" title="Jamaican Patois">
        Jamaican Patois
       </a>
       and
       <a href="/wiki/Jamaican_English" title="Jamaican English">
        Jamaican English
       </a>
      </div>
      <p>
       Jamaica is regarded as a
       <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Bilingual" title="Bilingual">
        bilingual
       </a>
       country, with two major languages in use by the population.
       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-62">
        <a href="#cite_note-62">
         [62]
        </a>
       </sup>
       The official language is
       <a href="/wiki/Jamaican_English" title="Jamaican English">
        Jamaican Standard English
       </a>
       (JSE) or Standard Jamaican English (SJE), which is "used in all domains of public life", including the government, the legal system, the media, and education.
       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-63">
        <a href="#cite_note-63">
         [63]
        </a>
       </sup>
       However, the primary spoken language is an
       <a href="/wiki/English-based_creole_languages" title="English-based creole languages">
        English-based creole
       </a>
       called
       <a href="/wiki/Jamaican_Patois" title="Jamaican Patois">
        Jamaican Patois
       </a>
       (or Patwa). A 2007 survey by the Jamaican Language Unit found that 17.1 percent of the population were
       <a href="/wiki/Monolingualism" title="Monolingualism">
        monolingual
       </a>
       in JSE, 36.5 percent were monolingual in Patois, and 46.4 percent were bilingual, although earlier surveys had pointed to a greater degree of bilinguality (up to 90 percent).
       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-64">
        <a href="#cite_note-64">
         [64]
        </a>
       </sup>
       The Jamaican education system has only recently begun to offer formal instruction in Patois, while retaining JSE as the "official language of instruction".
       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-65">
        <a href="#cite_note-65">
         [65]
        </a>
       </sup>
      </p>
      <p>
       Additionally, some Jamaicans use one or more of
       <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Jamaican_Sign_Language" title="Jamaican Sign Language">
        Jamaican Sign Language
       </a>
       ,
       <a href="/wiki/American_Sign_Language" title="American Sign Language">
        American Sign Language
       </a>
       or the indigenous
       <a href="/wiki/Jamaican_Country_Sign_Language" title="Jamaican Country Sign Language">
        Jamaican Country Sign Language
       </a>
       (Konchri Sain).
       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-:0_66-0">
        <a href="#cite_note-:0-66">
         [66]
        </a>
       </sup>
       Both JSL and ASL are rapidly replacing Konchri Sain for a variety of reasons.
       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-:0_66-1">
        <a href="#cite_note-:0-66">
         [66]
        </a>
       </sup>
      </p>
      <h3>
       <span class="mw-headline" id="Emigration">
        Emigration
       </span>
      </h3>
      <div class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable" role="note">
       Main article:
       <a href="/wiki/Jamaican_diaspora" title="Jamaican diaspora">
        Jamaican diaspora
       </a>
      </div>
      <p>
       Many Jamaicans have
       <a href="/wiki/Emigration" title="Emigration">
        emigrated
       </a>
       to other countries, especially to the United Kingdom, the United States, and Canada. In the case of the United States, about 20,000 Jamaicans per year are granted permanent residence.
       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-67">
        <a href="#cite_note-67">
         [67]
        </a>
       </sup>
       The great number of Jamaicans living abroad has become known as the
       <a href="/wiki/Jamaican_diaspora" title="Jamaican diaspora">
        Jamaican diaspora
       </a>
       . There has also been emigration of Jamaicans to
       <a href="/wiki/Cuba" title="Cuba">
        Cuba
       </a>
       .
       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-68">
        <a href="#cite_note-68">
         [68]
        </a>
       </sup>
       The scale of emigration has been widespread and similar to other Caribbean entities such as
       <a href="/wiki/Puerto_Rico" title="Puerto Rico">
        Puerto Rico
       </a>
       ,
       <a href="/wiki/Guyana" title="Guyana">
        Guyana
       </a>
       , and
       <a href="/wiki/The_Bahamas" title="The Bahamas">
        The Bahamas
       </a>
       . It was estimated in 2004 that up to 2.5 million Jamaicans and Jamaican descendants live abroad.
       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-69">
        <a href="#cite_note-69">
         [69]
        </a>
       </sup>
      </p>
      <p>
       <a href="/wiki/British_Jamaican" title="British Jamaican">
        Jamaicans in the United Kingdom
       </a>
       number an estimated 800,000 making them by far the country's largest
       <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/British_African-Caribbean_community" title="British African-Caribbean community">
        African-Caribbean group
       </a>
       . Large-scale migration from Jamaica to the UK occurred primarily in the 1950s and 1960s (when the country was still under British rule). Jamaican communities exist in most large UK cities.
       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-IOMMapping_70-0">
        <a href="#cite_note-IOMMapping-70">
         [70]
        </a>
       </sup>
       Concentrations of
       <a href="/wiki/Expatriate" title="Expatriate">
        expatriate
       </a>
       Jamaicans are quite considerable in numerous cities in the United States, including
       <a href="/wiki/New_York_City" title="New York City">
        New York City
       </a>
       ,
       <a href="/wiki/Buffalo,_New_York" title="Buffalo, New York">
        Buffalo
       </a>
       , the
       <a href="/wiki/South_Florida" title="South Florida">
        Miami
       </a>
       metro area,
       <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Atlanta,_Georgia" title="Atlanta, Georgia">
        Atlanta
       </a>
       ,
       <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Chicago,_Illinois" title="Chicago, Illinois">
        Chicago
       </a>
       ,
       <a href="/wiki/Orlando,_Florida" title="Orlando, Florida">
        Orlando
       </a>
       ,
       <a href="/wiki/Tampa,_Florida" title="Tampa, Florida">
        Tampa
       </a>
       ,
       <a href="/wiki/Washington,_D.C." title="Washington, D.C.">
        Washington, D.C.
       </a>
       ,
       <a href="/wiki/Philadelphia" title="Philadelphia">
        Philadelphia
       </a>
       ,
       <a href="/wiki/Hartford,_Connecticut" title="Hartford, Connecticut">
        Hartford
       </a>
       ,
       <a href="/wiki/Providence,_Rhode_Island" title="Providence, Rhode Island">
        Providence
       </a>
       and
       <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Los_Angeles,_California" title="Los Angeles, California">
        Los Angeles
       </a>
       . In Canada, the Jamaican population is centred in
       <a href="/wiki/Toronto" title="Toronto">
        Toronto
       </a>
       , and there are smaller communities in cities such as
       <a href="/wiki/Hamilton,_Ontario" title="Hamilton, Ontario">
        Hamilton
       </a>
       ,
       <a href="/wiki/Montreal" title="Montreal">
        Montreal
       </a>
       ,
       <a href="/wiki/Winnipeg" title="Winnipeg">
        Winnipeg
       </a>
       ,
       <a href="/wiki/Vancouver" title="Vancouver">
        Vancouver
       </a>
       and
       <a href="/wiki/Ottawa" title="Ottawa">
        Ottawa
       </a>
       .
      </p>
      <h3>
       <span class="mw-headline" id="Crime">
        Crime
       </span>
      </h3>
      <div class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable" role="note">
       Main article:
       <a href="/wiki/Crime_in_Jamaica" title="Crime in Jamaica">
        Crime in Jamaica
       </a>
      </div>
      <div class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable" role="note">
       See also:
       <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Prisons_in_Jamaica" title="Prisons in Jamaica">
        Prisons in Jamaica
       </a>
       and
       <a href="/wiki/LGBT_rights_in_Jamaica" title="LGBT rights in Jamaica">
        LGBT rights in Jamaica
       </a>
      </div>
      <p>
       When Jamaica gained independence in 1962, the murder rate was 3.9 per 100,000 inhabitants, one of the lowest in the world. By 2009, the rate was 62 per 100,000 inhabitants, one of the highest in the world.
       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-71">
        <a href="#cite_note-71">
         [71]
        </a>
       </sup>
       Jamaica has had one of the highest murder rates in the world for many years, according to
       <a href="/wiki/United_Nations" title="United Nations">
        UN
       </a>
       estimates.
       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Nationmaster_Crime_Stats_72-0">
        <a href="#cite_note-Nationmaster_Crime_Stats-72">
         [72]
        </a>
       </sup>
       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-un37820_73-0">
        <a href="#cite_note-un37820-73">
         [73]
        </a>
       </sup>
       Some areas of Jamaica, particularly cities such as Kingston, experience high levels of crime and violence.
       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-74">
        <a href="#cite_note-74">
         [74]
        </a>
       </sup>
       Some Jamaicans are hostile towards
       <a href="/wiki/LGBT" title="LGBT">
        LGBT
       </a>
       and intersex people,
       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-75">
        <a href="#cite_note-75">
         [75]
        </a>
       </sup>
       and there have been reported cases of mob attacks against gay people.
       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-NewYorkTimes_76-0">
        <a href="#cite_note-NewYorkTimes-76">
         [76]
        </a>
       </sup>
       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-HumanRightsWatch_77-0">
        <a href="#cite_note-HumanRightsWatch-77">
         [77]
        </a>
       </sup>
       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-AmnestyInternational_78-0">
        <a href="#cite_note-AmnestyInternational-78">
         [78]
        </a>
       </sup>
      </p>
      <p>
       However, there were 1,682 reported murders in 2009 and 1,428 in 2010.
       <sup class="noprint Inline-Template Template-Fact" style="white-space:nowrap;">
        [
        <i>
         <a href="/wiki/Wikipedia:Citation_needed" title="Wikipedia:Citation needed">
          <span title="This claim needs references to reliable sources. (December 2017)">
           citation needed
          </span>
         </a>
        </i>
        ]
       </sup>
       Since 2011 the murder rate continued to fall following the downward trend in 2010 after a strategic programme was launched.
       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-79">
        <a href="#cite_note-79">
         [79]
        </a>
       </sup>
       In 2012, the Ministry of National Security reported a 30 percent decrease in murders.
       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-80">
        <a href="#cite_note-80">
         [80]
        </a>
       </sup>
       Nevertheless, in 2017 murders rose by 22% over the previous year.
       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-81">
        <a href="#cite_note-81">
         [81]
        </a>
       </sup>
      </p>

      <h2>
       <span class="mw-headline" id="Religion">
        Religion
       </span>
      </h2>
      <div class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable" role="note">
       Main article:
       <a href="/wiki/Religion_in_Jamaica" title="Religion in Jamaica">
        Religion in Jamaica
       </a>
      </div>
      <div class="thumb tright">
       <div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;">
        <a class="image" href="/wiki/File:Mandeville_Church_by_AAlexander.jpg">
         <img alt="" class="thumbimage" data-file-height="750" data-file-width="1000" height="165" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/9/93/Mandeville_Church_by_AAlexander.jpg/220px-Mandeville_Church_by_AAlexander.jpg" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/9/93/Mandeville_Church_by_AAlexander.jpg/330px-Mandeville_Church_by_AAlexander.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/9/93/Mandeville_Church_by_AAlexander.jpg/440px-Mandeville_Church_by_AAlexander.jpg 2x" width="220"/>
        </a>
        <div class="thumbcaption">
         <div class="magnify">
          <a class="internal" href="/wiki/File:Mandeville_Church_by_AAlexander.jpg" title="Enlarge">
          </a>
         </div>
         Mandeville Church (est. 1816), an
         <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Anglican" title="Anglican">
          Anglican
         </a>
         church in
         <a href="/wiki/Manchester_Parish" title="Manchester Parish">
          Manchester Parish
         </a>
        </div>
       </div>
      </div>
      <p>
       <a href="/wiki/Christianity" title="Christianity">
        Christianity
       </a>
       is the largest religion practised in Jamaica.
       <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Protestants" title="Protestants">
        Protestants
       </a>
       form the majority of approximately 70% in the country, and
       <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Roman_Catholics" title="Roman Catholics">
        Roman Catholics
       </a>
       are a minority with 2% of the population. According to the 2001 census, the country's largest Protestant denominations are the
       <a href="/wiki/Church_of_God_(Anderson,_Indiana)" title="Church of God (Anderson, Indiana)">
        Church of God
       </a>
       (24%),
       <a href="/wiki/Seventh-day_Adventist_Church" title="Seventh-day Adventist Church">
        Seventh-day Adventist Church
       </a>
       (11%),
       <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Pentecostal" title="Pentecostal">
        Pentecostal
       </a>
       (10%),
       <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Baptist" title="Baptist">
        Baptist
       </a>
       (7%),
       <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Anglican" title="Anglican">
        Anglican
       </a>
       (4%),
       <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/United_Church" title="United Church">
        United Church
       </a>
       (2%),
       <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Methodist" title="Methodist">
        Methodist
       </a>
       (2%),
       <a href="/wiki/Moravian_Church" title="Moravian Church">
        Moravian
       </a>
       (1%) and
       <a href="/wiki/Plymouth_Brethren" title="Plymouth Brethren">
        Plymouth Brethren
       </a>
       (1%)
       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-state2007_82-0">
        <a href="#cite_note-state2007-82">
         [82]
        </a>
       </sup>
       The Christian faith gained acceptance as British Christian abolitionists and Baptist missionaries joined educated former slaves in the struggle against slavery.
       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-83">
        <a href="#cite_note-83">
         [83]
        </a>
       </sup>
      </p>
      <p>
       The
       <a href="/wiki/Rastafari" title="Rastafari">
        Rastafari movement
       </a>
       has 29,026 adherents, according to the 2011 census, with 25,325 Rastafarian males and 3,701 Rastafarian females.
       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-state2007_82-1">
        <a href="#cite_note-state2007-82">
         [82]
        </a>
       </sup>
       Other religions in Jamaica include
       <a href="/wiki/Jehovah%27s_Witnesses" title="Jehovah's Witnesses">
        Jehovah's Witnesses
       </a>
       (2% population), the
       <a href="/wiki/Bah%C3%A1%27%C3%AD_Faith_in_Jamaica" title="Bahá'í Faith in Jamaica">
        Bahá'í faith
       </a>
       , which counts perhaps 8,000 adherents
       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-84">
        <a href="#cite_note-84">
         [84]
        </a>
       </sup>
       and 21
       <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Local_Spiritual_Assembly" title="Local Spiritual Assembly">
        Local Spiritual Assemblies
       </a>
       ,
       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-4th_85-0">
        <a href="#cite_note-4th-85">
         [85]
        </a>
       </sup>
       <a href="/wiki/Buddhism" title="Buddhism">
        Buddhism
       </a>
       , and
       <a href="/wiki/Hinduism" title="Hinduism">
        Hinduism
       </a>
       .
       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-86">
        <a href="#cite_note-86">
         [86]
        </a>
       </sup>
       There is a small population of
       <a href="/wiki/Judaism" title="Judaism">
        Jews
       </a>
       , about 200, who describe themselves as Liberal-Conservative.
       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-87">
        <a href="#cite_note-87">
         [87]
        </a>
       </sup>
       The first Jews in Jamaica trace their roots back to early 15th century Spain and Portugal.
       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-88">
        <a href="#cite_note-88">
         [88]
        </a>
       </sup>
       Other small groups include
       <a href="/wiki/Islam" title="Islam">
        Muslims
       </a>
       , who claim 5,000 adherents,
       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-state2007_82-2">
        <a href="#cite_note-state2007-82">
         [82]
        </a>
       </sup>
       as do the Mormons.
       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-89">
        <a href="#cite_note-89">
         [89]
        </a>
       </sup>
      </p>

       </span>
